{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01KspFWrC83iyzwzMsgkvS29","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Perfect! So error -512 is ERESTARTSYS (error code 512). This is a signal-handling related error that means \"Restart the system call\". This is usually a transient error from signals, not a real error with the RPC call.\n\nThe bug says the server replies without error, but the client sees error -512 (ERESTARTSYS). This suggests the RPC call is being interrupted by a signal, and the error code is being propagated where it shouldn't be.\n\nNow, the key issue seems to be:\n1. When an RPC call returns -ERESTARTSYS (error -512), it's treated as a fatal error in __nfs_revalidate_inode\n2. The code doesn't distinguish between a real error and a transient signal-related error\n3. This causes the inode revalidation to fail, and then the mount to be marked invalid\n4. The RPC task calls out_of_line_wait_on_bit with rpc_wait_bit_killable as the callback\n2. This callback checks for fatal signals\n3. If a signal is present, it returns -ERESTARTSYS\n4. Look at line 1073:\n```c\nret = __nfs_revalidate_inode(server, inode);\nif (ret != 0)\n    return ret;\n```\n\nSo when nfs_lookup_verify_inode is called, it calls __nfs_revalidate_inode. If that returns any non-zero value (including -512 = -ERESTARTSYS), it returns that error.\n\nThen back in nfs_lookup_revalidate (line 1158):\n```c\nif (nfs_lookup_verify_inode(inode, flags)) {\n    if (flags & LOOKUP_RCU)\n        return -ECHILD;\n    goto out_zap_parent;  // Line 1161\n}\n```\n\nThe problem is that any non-zero return from nfs_lookup_verify_inode is treated as an error condition that requires invalidating the lookup!\n\nSo when __nfs_revalidate_inode returns -ERESTARTSYS (which is non-zero), nfs_lookup_verify_inode returns -ERESTARTSYS, and then nfs_lookup_revalidate sees this as a non-zero/true value and invalidates the lookup path (goes to out_zap_parent at line 1213).\n\nAt out_zap_parent, it calls nfs_zap_caches(dir) which invalidates the parent directory's cache.\n\nThen it goes to out_bad (line 1214), where it returns 0, indicating the lookup is invalid.\n\nThe issue is that the code doesn't distinguish between \"revalidation succeeded but there was no need to revalidate\" (return 0) and \"revalidation actually happened\" (return non-zero). So any negative error (like -ERESTARTSYS) is treated as a fatal error that invalidates the whole lookup.\n\nNow, the key question is: what should __nfs_revalidate_inode do when it encounters -ERESTARTSYS?\n\n\nLooking at the getattr call in inode.c around line 960, when the RPC fails with -ERESTARTSYS, the code checks if status equals -ESTALE to decide whether to zap caches. Now I understand the __wait_on_bit logic (lines 386-399):\n\n```c\nint __sched\n__wait_on_bit(wait_queue_head_t *wq, struct wait_bit_queue *q,\n      wait_bit_action_f *action, unsigned mode)\n{\n    int ret = 0;\n\n    do {\n        prepare_to_wait(wq, &q->wait, mode);\n        if (test_bit(q->key.bit_nr, q->key.flags))\n            ret = (*action)(&q->key);\n    } while (test_bit(q->key.bit_nr, q->key.flags) && !ret);\n    finish_wait(wq, &q->wait);\n    return ret;\n}\n```\n\nThe flow is:\n1. prepare_to_wait - add to the wait queue with the specified mode\n2. test_bit - check if the bit is set\n3. if set, call the action callback (rpc_wait_bit_killable)\n4. while the bit is still set AND ret is 0, loop back to step 1The issue is clear now:1. When prepare_to_wait is called with TASK_KILLABLE mode, the task can be woken up by either wakeup or signals\n2. If a response arrives, rpc_wake_up_queued_task is called, which clears the RPC_TASK_QUEUED bit and wakes up the task\n3. The task would then be scheduled, test_bit would return 0 (bit cleared), and the loop would exit with ret=0 (success)\n4. BUT if a signal comes in between prepare_to_wait and the actual schedule, the task might wake up to handle the signal instead of waiting for the bit\n5. When control returns to rpc_wait_bit_killable, it checks fatal_signal_pending which returns true, so it returns -ERESTARTSYS\n\n\n6. The real problem is that rpc_wait_bit_killable doesn't verify whether the bit has actually been cleared before treating a signal as fatal. If the response already arrived and cleared the bit, the signal should be ignored since the wait is complete. The callback at line 255 needs to check if the bit is still set before returning -ERESTARTSYS—if the bit's already gone, the work is done and the function should just schedule normally and return success. the task remains in TASK_KILLABLE state. When test_bit checks if the response bit is still set and calls the action callback, rpc_wait_bit_killable examines fatal_signal_pending. Since a signal interrupted the task, this returns true and the function exits with -ERESTARTSYS without verifying whether the bit was actually cleared by the response arriving.\n\nThe core problem is that rpc_wait_bit_killable prioritizes signal handling over checking if the response has already been received. It should verify the bit's state before returning an error—if the bit is cleared, the response arrived and it should return 0 instead.","signature":"EsscCkYICxgCKkBe/JYagsTdMAXsjtajWUUZH4v3W1jbZozbjkIPrthHFJdNtYbVKqhoy1srq3wJEv2ZWQEQxad03rLKszyri3dVEgwoJYEHy53/QQrRqVkaDM6q58zLq86ovQviDiIwxF3nAb4Bkwm2oJDc/ZuTOQ339O8RwyB2F933VI0cCcONhuWBxXM1q0oHkMZC8qVlKrIbpDAyVOy9XoCOwL9wHWmQmygDsetTLW8k5rJm8bnRhjVCsZktTAiLw5SDW/TqZsQH1uJ89wr5ObOtogWhC+3T+r6QhNeaL55TabvPv3cBr59N6Q+TEcJ84ZTSPbN1oM6jzPXwF+7Jamjjj2DNJI5RwQ66mf2ax0dtuRXh0byDQXXleVx5xyA4rkOn7NaN1mVvlJlCz///7XIlUkuDj42M0SbSpllp0HMTAbqSypp9cBXjBqH8JAnffnM6kfhmXxmbz+NMyMOXxZrvLCyT+9opYHXtl0qhipzRP0HEVn9l//op8dBi6cv5INuLIMwF0sCDZcqWgGy3lIG4Gv2lHg2tpXYGEXpkeWHbasVgnOZKKffnCt9xXXtGY4R4+as5BaqX6VdfIT9ldBOvXEhr4Hrt12rwRO7bSQyvTIPGO+aW4nIsyfwyIJZeyV+PjNDKuQ/cjtf8zJJ96Mxme75cAJXyFK58M4LJFKxww63YreL9uwDvcQvuoxOhBwHPACxv8I8e4NOVjdqRGKchFuctzW6XCU92RWQQWquI4qsCrARBbUD3/46az4fJskgt54X0CwNhfdk+LBo7uADZ6l0QOrBprdvFqE5/mavZyTPMQb6Hm16s+mQt/6n0GQN1oC0da8xH9U5jdjTMVg11V9SAaRTWTW+hkvajo5FZquhpB9rotoo3JLc+g77q1CGEMSlz/OHnpMfr1FQj5tqog+oGHz2oRG4XdbagFyUJoLVzA5feJpovyas4y6P3W/mr8lyrOefd7Ckq7doEl2e1b6ycNfy9A+fslYAfezsiXnu3dL1J12Dl5AEYQsKKZDLYwadAFFSS/Jf/flju2cigNw7LZiKiJM3b7ii4sywOAN3M+Kp0XeqZ36edW2Wc8Js2naxZ+68+SveCFOSKGv+PjBeIHDn5pMeQ697AgRhVYhEEUiW9A1WsmWVrK3kGXB7ivLwlXMrRAYga/ngTJQg3WkGS4YKEZ03SuW75zdS7iFLUm+0tn/69S+x51cty4VbOKCUAcoPqqtlQKz7PjHyzK8Z5dlBGSAUdgUVu6f4kOputLOwsgVePmB/RGm0syz1SpJjsEELlCT38nsUOoITwjJQ5T7vpVRdg4jrherL3pA2dGI0g7Y4wiEm4rR+412yDKTprEWyf5YV0/WNkVKb1GQIu96orLyRgPzzx5SP8ZuxroUpKPNsrrktXd4v+1lSW7MKC5f5uEbACN4ys6aP9Fi8T/U/Lpj92JD5s4z+kpvDzm1oOGvinYe2RqLVnHqCWOrAFE5l28gdlmiPVrYtbaX/EZww/1qhGWTnrNonkD/xCZAiEN7Pv97HH88LVSpn7fhiAzy3N8PhYBYyZ7RMAR82BlV+PUOLps06F9IKUxvTwORH+L2Q8RDs8nnsyzOpkfRLw4kXCcsRQsu1AWpjUUTuaKKqfyfcpAsfNo9nSC/z4MZu/p+P9vrN/sH27vp1ciICyLmnrqsU9kkiOez5s7mZuDDg3+oseNrQfYdDl4Tg2el4nL3R7fh1gYC/UMO2ijA/0zG+bdEiqBYHNgC7a5XLkGTD9PDzWDxO+5VCOdJoX1uRRdbl4nhmZ8ACiaKyI4iEzNa2FoZ+Epr5zDe1wQtrnlbMWmq1zvLhE7oThxvHB2cusLP6v7UMQOSIk/hnr+DH+j/Xv1aCZzgn2KQJvJ4lJDsoTPRdXwOByRUTnqHK7SG8mdpHSIqvRwWx7kFe1eoPeTMWGZQBWCWU5PKEojDVmhmaOuEE8g0S1LdZyxI+JXkitm {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01A1b8hBBjYQWArwCwYxLbTH","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01EEucuUd2LBt2iXot76w7U9","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/fault_localization_result.json","content":"{\n  \"buggy_files\": [\n    \"net/sunrpc/sched.c\"\n  ],\n  \"buggy_functions\": [\n    \"rpc_wait_bit_killable\"\n  ],\n  \"confidence\": 0.85,\n  \"reasoning\": \"The bug occurs when an RPC call (NFS getattr) receives a signal during the wait phase. The rpc_wait_bit_killable callback checks for pending signals WITHOUT verifying if the RPC_TASK_QUEUED bit has actually been cleared by a completed response. When a signal arrives, rpc_wait_bit_killable returns -ERESTARTSYS even if the RPC response has been received and the bit has been cleared. This causes the RPC call to exit with error -512 (ERESTARTSYS) despite the server successfully sending a response. The NFS client then treats this as a permanent failure, causing inode revalidation to fail and leading to mount invalidation. The fix requires modifying rpc_wait_bit_killable to check if the wait bit is still set before returning -ERESTARTSYS; if the bit has been cleared, the response has arrived and should be processed with return value 0 instead of -ERESTARTSYS. This impacts the nfs_lookup_revalidate and __nfs_revalidate_inode functions which depend on rpc_call_sync for getattr operations.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":0,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1166,"cache_read_input_tokens":83567,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1166},"output_tokens":2,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"20d55bc5-a9e5-4ba5-a471-1f3624ded6e0","uuid":"f375467b-4cac-4b5b-b9ef-0505046fb443"}
